<p>September 2015</p> <p>Volume 30 Number 9</p> <h1 id=3D"the-working-programmer---how-to-be-mean-nodejs">The Working Progr= ammer - How To Be MEAN: Node.js</h1> <p>By <a href=3D"https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/archive/msdn-magazine/201= 5/september/%5Carchive%5Cmsdn-magazine%5Cauthors%5CTed_Neward" data-linktyp= e=3D"relative-path">Ted Neward</a> | September 2015</p> <p><img src=3D"https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/archive/msdn-magazine/2015/= september/images/mt422588.ted_neward_headshot(en-us,msdn.10).jpg" alt=3D"Te= d Neward" title=3D"Ted Neward" data-linktype=3D"relative-path">Microsoft ha= s been adopting technology from across the software spectrum as part of its= rebranding and =E2=80=9Cre-relevancing.=E2=80=9D One of the technologies i= t has adopted is Node.js. This gives developers a golden opportunity to use= one of the more popular full-stack software groupings on the Node.js platf= orm known as MEAN: MongoDB, Express, AngularJS and Node.js.</p> <p>In the last installment (<a href=3D"http://msdn.microsoft.com/magazine/m= t185576" data-linktype=3D"external">msdn.microsoft.com/magazine/mt185576</a= >), I got the basic Node.js parts up and running. In this one, I=E2=80=99ll= spin up a simple Node =E2=80=9CHello World=E2=80=9D Web endpoint, and depl= oy it to a Microsoft Azure Web site. Over the next several installments, I= =E2=80=99ll slowly build my way through the MEAN stack, working from the gr= ound up.</p> <p>As discussed in the previous article, there are a lot of places where I = could swap out parts of the MEAN stack for something else=E2=80=94DocumentD= B for MongoDB, ASP.NET WebAPI for Node.js and ASP.NET MVC for Express, or B= ackboneJS (or any of a whole host of other JavaScript Single-Page-Applicati= on frameworks) for AngularJS=E2=80=94but none of the alternatives enjoys th= e popularity that MEAN currently holds (at least among JavaScript aficionad= os).</p> <h2 id=3D"nodejs" class=3D"heading-anchor"><a class=3D"anchor-link docon do= con-link" href=3D"https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/archive/msdn-magazine/20= 15/september/the-working-programmer-how-to-be-mean-node-js#nodejs" aria-lab= elledby=3D"nodejs"></a>Node.js</h2> <p>Node.js is fundamentally just =E2=80=9CJavaScript on the server.=E2=80= =9D Yes, there=E2=80=99s a different programming approach to Node.js that t= ries to deal with concurrent execution. Instead of block on a call, the pro= grammer passes in a function literal to be invoked when the operation is co= mpleted. This lets the developer to think of code as single-threaded, even = though multiple threads are in use below the surface. On the whole, though,= the largest distinction of Node.js is you use JavaScript to build the serv= er components, instead of C#, Java or Ruby. In that sense, it=E2=80=99s rea= lly just a change of scenery=E2=80=94not an entirely different universe.</p= > <p>The simplest Node.js application is, of course, the ubiquitous =E2=80=9C= Hello, World,=E2=80=9D which you can easily write using the built-in consol= e object:</p> <div class=3D"codeHeader" id=3D"code-try-0" data-bi-name=3D"code-header"><s= pan class=3D"language">XML</span><button type=3D"button" class=3D"action po= sition-relative" data-bi-name=3D"copy" aria-label=3D"Copy code"> <span class=3D"icon"> <span class=3D"docon docon-edit-copy" role=3D"presentation"></span> </span> <span>Copy</span> <div class=3D"successful-copy-alert position-absolute right-0 top-0 lef= t-0 bottom-0 display-flex align-items-center justify-content-center has-tex= t-success-invert has-background-success is-transparent" aria-hidden=3D"true= "> <span class=3D"icon font-size-l"> <span class=3D"docon docon-check-mark" role=3D"presentation"></span> </span> </div> </button></div><pre tabindex=3D"0" class=3D"has-inner-focus"><code class= =3D"lang-xml" data-author-content=3D"console.log("Howdy, NodeJS!"= ); "><span>console.log("Howdy, NodeJS!"); </span></code></pre> <p>Assuming this goes into a file called hello.js in the current directory,= you=E2=80=99d run it using the node utility at the command-line using node= hello.js. Or you could let Node.js infer the filename extension by simply = running =E2=80=9Cnode hello.=E2=80=9D Either way, Node greets you in the tr= aditional way.</p> <p>Like most programming platforms, Node.js has its own set of libraries an= d APIs out of the box. As I pointed out last time, Node.js uses the require= convention to reference an installed library. This traps the returned obje= ct into a local variable of the same name. So, for example, if I want to wr= ite a simple HTTP server that will effectively give me the same greeting ov= er the HTTP protocol, I can put the following into a simple helloHTTP.js fi= le:</p> <div class=3D"codeHeader" id=3D"code-try-1" data-bi-name=3D"code-header"><s= pan class=3D"language">JavaScript</span><button type=3D"button" class=3D"ac= tion position-relative" data-bi-name=3D"copy" aria-label=3D"Copy code"> <span class=3D"icon"> <span class=3D"docon docon-edit-copy" role=3D"presentation"></span> </span> <span>Copy</span> <div class=3D"successful-copy-alert position-absolute right-0 top-0 lef= t-0 bottom-0 display-flex align-items-center justify-content-center has-tex= t-success-invert has-background-success is-transparent" aria-hidden=3D"true= "> <span class=3D"icon font-size-l"> <span class=3D"docon docon-check-mark" role=3D"presentation"></span> </span> </div> </button></div><pre tabindex=3D"0" class=3D"has-inner-focus"><code class= =3D"lang-javascript" data-author-content=3D"var http =3D require('http'); var port =3D process.env.PORT || 3000; http.createServer(function(req, res) {   res.writeHead(200, { 'Content-Type': 'text/plain' });   res.end('Hello World\n'); }).listen(port); "><span><span class=3D"hljs-keyword">var</span> http =3D <span class=3D"hlj= s-built_in">require</span>(<span class=3D"hljs-string">'http'</span>); <span class=3D"hljs-keyword">var</span> port =3D process.env.PORT || <span = class=3D"hljs-number">3000</span>; http.createServer(<span class=3D"hljs-function"><span class=3D"hljs-keyword= ">function</span>(<span class=3D"hljs-params">req, res</span>) </span>{   res.writeHead(<span class=3D"hljs-number">200</span>, { <span class= =3D"hljs-string">'Content-Type'</span>: <span class=3D"hljs-string">'text/p= lain'</span> });   res.end(<span class=3D"hljs-string">'Hello World\n'</span>); }).listen(port); </span></code></pre> <p>The require line finds the =E2=80=9Chttp=E2=80=9D library within the Nod= e.js installation, and stores it to the http object in dependency injection= . This is a standard Node.js convention, and should be held as fairly sacro= sanct. The second line uses the built-in process object to access the surro= unding environment. In this case, it uses the =E2=80=9Cenv=E2=80=9D object = within the process object to determine whether an environment variable name= d PORT is set to anything. If it is, I=E2=80=99ll use that as the port on w= hich to run the server. Otherwise, I=E2=80=99ll use the default port 3000. = Many Node.js frameworks prefer port 3000 as the default, for obscure histor= ical and cultural reasons.</p> <p>The nature of Node.js programming becomes clearer in the next few lines.= I use the http object to create an HTTP server. The sole parameter is a fu= nction literal that takes a req (HTTP request) object and a res (HTTP respo= nse) object as parameters, and uses res to write the HTTP response back. Th= is idiom is ubiquitous throughout all levels of the Node.js stack.</p> <p>This is one of those =E2=80=9Cyou love it or you hate it=E2=80=9D kinds = of things. You=E2=80=99ll be seeing more of this in the articles to come. S= o if this isn=E2=80=99t clear, spend some time experimenting. The returned = object from createServer is then bound to the desired port using the listen= call. Lo and behold, you have a running HTTP server you can easily run usi= ng =E2=80=9Cnode helloHTTP=E2=80=9D and pointing a browser at http://localh= ost:3000.</p> <h2 id=3D"azure-command-line-tools" class=3D"heading-anchor"><a class=3D"an= chor-link docon docon-link" href=3D"https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/archiv= e/msdn-magazine/2015/september/the-working-programmer-how-to-be-mean-node-j= s#azure-command-line-tools" aria-labelledby=3D"azure-command-line-tools"></= a>Azure Command-Line Tools</h2> <p>From my last article, you=E2=80=99ll recall Node.js has a package utilit= y called the Node package manager (npm) you can use to download dependent l= ibraries. You can also use it to download tools you can then use from the c= ommand line. This is a subtle, but powerful, aspect of Node.js. It acts as = a platform-neutral =E2=80=9Cplaying field equalizer.=E2=80=9D</p> <p>You can effectively hide any distinctions between Windows, Mac OS or Lin= ux behind a wall of JavaScript scripts. Microsoft picked up on this a while= back, and packaged a set of command-line tools into a Node.js package call= ed azure-cli. Installing it is easy with npm:</p> <div class=3D"codeHeader" id=3D"code-try-2" data-bi-name=3D"code-header"><s= pan class=3D"language">XML</span><button type=3D"button" class=3D"action po= sition-relative" data-bi-name=3D"copy" aria-label=3D"Copy code"> <span class=3D"icon"> <span class=3D"docon docon-edit-copy" role=3D"presentation"></span> </span> <span>Copy</span> <div class=3D"successful-copy-alert position-absolute right-0 top-0 lef= t-0 bottom-0 display-flex align-items-center justify-content-center has-tex= t-success-invert has-background-success is-transparent" aria-hidden=3D"true= "> <span class=3D"icon font-size-l"> <span class=3D"docon docon-check-mark" role=3D"presentation"></span> </span> </div> </button></div><pre tabindex=3D"0" class=3D"has-inner-focus"><code class= =3D"lang-xml" data-author-content=3D"npm install =E2=80=93g azure-cli "><span>npm install =E2=80=93g azure-cli </span></code></pre> <p>The -g flag tells npm to install the tools =E2=80=9Cglobally=E2=80=9D (m= eaning they=E2=80=99re not tied to the local directory in which the command= is run). This makes the resulting package available for use across the ent= ire system. When it=E2=80=99s finished, a new command-line utility, azure, = will be available for use. The azure-cli package doesn=E2=80=99t give any g= reater or lesser functionality than using the Azure Portal. The azure-cli t= ool=E2=80=99s advantage lies in its ability to script azure commands as par= t of an automated deploy system, for example.</p> <h2 id=3D"deploy-to-azure" class=3D"heading-anchor"><a class=3D"anchor-link= docon docon-link" href=3D"https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/archive/msdn-ma= gazine/2015/september/the-working-programmer-how-to-be-mean-node-js#deploy-= to-azure" aria-labelledby=3D"deploy-to-azure"></a>Deploy to Azure</h2> <p>So, if you want this lovely little greeting to be available to the world= over the Internet, you need to create an Azure Web Site as a host. Using t= he =E2=80=9Cazure=E2=80=9D tool, it=E2=80=99s pretty simple. First, you hav= e to tie the tool in to the account in Azure:</p> <div class=3D"codeHeader" id=3D"code-try-3" data-bi-name=3D"code-header"><s= pan class=3D"language">XML</span><button type=3D"button" class=3D"action po= sition-relative" data-bi-name=3D"copy" aria-label=3D"Copy code"> <span class=3D"icon"> <span class=3D"docon docon-edit-copy" role=3D"presentation"></span> </span> <span>Copy</span> <div class=3D"successful-copy-alert position-absolute right-0 top-0 lef= t-0 bottom-0 display-flex align-items-center justify-content-center has-tex= t-success-invert has-background-success is-transparent" aria-hidden=3D"true= "> <span class=3D"icon font-size-l"> <span class=3D"docon docon-check-mark" role=3D"presentation"></span> </span> </div> </button></div><pre tabindex=3D"0" class=3D"has-inner-focus"><code class= =3D"lang-xml" data-author-content=3D"azure account download "><span>azure account download </span></code></pre> <p>This will fire up the system=E2=80=99s default browser pointing to the A= zure login portal. Use the Azure account credentials to log in. When you=E2= =80=99re done, it will automatically download a publishSettings file contai= ning the credential information the azure tool needs, which can be directly= imported:</p> <div class=3D"codeHeader" id=3D"code-try-4" data-bi-name=3D"code-header"><s= pan class=3D"language">XML</span><button type=3D"button" class=3D"action po= sition-relative" data-bi-name=3D"copy" aria-label=3D"Copy code"> <span class=3D"icon"> <span class=3D"docon docon-edit-copy" role=3D"presentation"></span> </span> <span>Copy</span> <div class=3D"successful-copy-alert position-absolute right-0 top-0 lef= t-0 bottom-0 display-flex align-items-center justify-content-center has-tex= t-success-invert has-background-success is-transparent" aria-hidden=3D"true= "> <span class=3D"icon font-size-l"> <span class=3D"docon docon-check-mark" role=3D"presentation"></span> </span> </div> </button></div><pre tabindex=3D"0" class=3D"has-inner-focus"><code class= =3D"lang-xml" data-author-content=3D"azure account import <filename> "><span>azure account import <span class=3D"hljs-tag"><<span class=3D"hl= js-name">filename</span>></span> </span></code></pre> <p>Filename will often be something like =E2=80=9CVisual Studio Ultimate wi= th MSDN-4-23-2015-credentials.publishsettings,=E2=80=9D depending on the Az= ure subscription details and the date you download the publishSettings file= . Once that=E2=80=99s done, it=E2=80=99s a simple matter to create a new Az= ure Web site by setting up Git to do deployments to the site:</p> <div class=3D"codeHeader" id=3D"code-try-5" data-bi-name=3D"code-header"><s= pan class=3D"language">XML</span><button type=3D"button" class=3D"action po= sition-relative" data-bi-name=3D"copy" aria-label=3D"Copy code"> <span class=3D"icon"> <span class=3D"docon docon-edit-copy" role=3D"presentation"></span> </span> <span>Copy</span> <div class=3D"successful-copy-alert position-absolute right-0 top-0 lef= t-0 bottom-0 display-flex align-items-center justify-content-center has-tex= t-success-invert has-background-success is-transparent" aria-hidden=3D"true= "> <span class=3D"icon font-size-l"> <span class=3D"docon docon-check-mark" role=3D"presentation"></span> </span> </div> </button></div><pre tabindex=3D"0" class=3D"has-inner-focus"><code class= =3D"lang-xml" data-author-content=3D"azure site create =E2=80=93git "><span>azure site create =E2=80=93git </span></code></pre> <p>This will prompt for a site name, and (assuming that name is unique) spi= n up the appropriate Web site. If all that works, spin up the current direc= tory as a git-initialized local repository. Assuming you=E2=80=99re still i= n the same directory that holds the helloHTTP.js file from before, you can = add it to the Git repository and push it to the Azure cloud:</p> <div class=3D"codeHeader" id=3D"code-try-6" data-bi-name=3D"code-header"><s= pan class=3D"language">XML</span><button type=3D"button" class=3D"action po= sition-relative" data-bi-name=3D"copy" aria-label=3D"Copy code"> <span class=3D"icon"> <span class=3D"docon docon-edit-copy" role=3D"presentation"></span> </span> <span>Copy</span> <div class=3D"successful-copy-alert position-absolute right-0 top-0 lef= t-0 bottom-0 display-flex align-items-center justify-content-center has-tex= t-success-invert has-background-success is-transparent" aria-hidden=3D"true= "> <span class=3D"icon font-size-l"> <span class=3D"docon docon-check-mark" role=3D"presentation"></span> </span> </div> </button></div><pre tabindex=3D"0" class=3D"has-inner-focus"><code class= =3D"lang-xml" data-author-content=3D"git add helloHTTP.js git commit =E2=80=93m "Initial commit" git push azure master "><span>git add helloHTTP.js git commit =E2=80=93m "Initial commit" git push azure master </span></code></pre> <p>Git will think about it for a few seconds. Then it will go through a seq= uence of steps that remain opaque for the moment. When it=E2=80=99s finishe= d, though, Azure will hold the new Node.js code, and you can browse to it, = as shown in <strong>Figure 1</strong>.</p> <p><img src=3D"https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/archive/msdn-magazine/2015/= september/images/mt422588.newardworkprog0915fig1_hires(en-us,msdn.10).png" = alt=3D"Hello, Node World" title=3D"Hello, Node World" data-linktype=3D"rela= tive-path"><br> <strong>Figure 1 Hello, Node World</strong></p> <p>This is why the helloHTTP code uses either the default port 3000 or the = environment variable PORT from the surrounding process. On the Azure cloud,= PORT is set to a value the Azure infrastructure maintains. This is so Micr= osoft can manage the various service endpoints more efficiently.</p> <p>That=E2=80=99s really the last of the installation steps you need to do.= Honestly, it takes longer to read about it than it does to actually run th= e commands, once you=E2=80=99re past the initial setup stages. And even mor= e honestly, any Azure work or exploration will require similar kinds of set= up. Azure really represents a next-step platform for many development effor= ts. In other words, this is something you=E2=80=99ll need to know how to do= eventually, so you may as well learn about it now.</p> <p>From here, pretty much everything will be MEAN-related. The only time yo= u=E2=80=99ll need to bring Azure details to mind is when you need to config= ure the environment to point to the MongoDB database server, for example, o= r when dealing with how Azure interacts with Node.js.</p> <h2 id=3D"wrapping-up" class=3D"heading-anchor"><a class=3D"anchor-link doc= on docon-link" href=3D"https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/archive/msdn-magazi= ne/2015/september/the-working-programmer-how-to-be-mean-node-js#wrapping-up= " aria-labelledby=3D"wrapping-up"></a>Wrapping Up</h2> <p>It=E2=80=99s worth pointing out that Node.js isn=E2=80=99t just an HTTP = pipeline. In fact, Node can run any kind of networked application by openin= g up the right library. The same is true of the Microsoft .NET Framework. H= owever, like the .NET Framework, most Node.js applications are going to be = HTTP-based in nature.</p> <p>The http library in Node.js is pretty low-level. As a result, the Node.j= s community developed a higher-level library and set of abstractions to mak= e dealing with HTTP-based endpoints easier. This library is called Express.= It lets you build what the Node.js community calls =E2=80=9Cmiddleware.=E2= =80=9D That=E2=80=99s what I=E2=80=99ll be looking at next time.</p> <p>For now, experiment with the Node.js http library, but don=E2=80=99t get= too attached, because I=E2=80=99ll be leaving it behind pretty quickly onc= e I get into the next iteration. In the meantime, however =E2=80=A6</p> <p>Happy coding.</p> <hr> <p><strong>Ted Neward</strong> <em>is the CTO at iTrellis, a consultin= g services company. He has written more than 100 articles and authored or c= o-authored a dozen books, including =E2=80=9CProfessional F# 2.0=E2=80=9D (= Wrox, 2010). He is an F# MVP and speaks at conferences around the world. He= consults and mentors regularly=E2=80=94reach him at <a href=3D"mailto:ted@= tedneward.com" data-linktype=3D"external">ted@tedneward.com</a> or <a href= =3D"mailto:ted@itrellis.com" data-linktype=3D"external">ted@itrellis.com</a= > if you=E2=80=99re interested.</em></p> <p>Thanks to the following technical expert for reviewing this article: Sha= wn Wildermuth<br> Shawn Wildermuth is a thirteen-time Microsoft MVP (ASP.NET/IIS), the author= of eight books and dozens of articles on software development, and a Plura= lsight author with over fifteen courses to his name.
